  549. Yes, Norelco fans, the demise of newer head compatibility and the handy little coffin have been greatly exaggerated.<br />Your 10**x shaver and the coffin case, like mine, can be salvaged and upgraded to 12**x performance for $50 and 10 minutes of your time.<br />The RQ12 SensoTouch 3d replacement heads fits my 1060x perfectly and shaves like a dream.<br />Many naysayers have complained that the newer head does not fit the coffin case. This is NOT TRUE! Sure, it is a little snug, but it does fit. After all, the case is lined with rubber.<br />Now, if you want the RQ12 mounted Arcitec to fit very smoothly into the coffin, just remove a little of the rubber. You can use a dental laboratory hand piece with a rotary, rough-cut stone, like I did, or you can use a Dremel or similar instrument to shave off approximately 0.3mm of rubber in the obvious two areas. Lacking that, get ahold of some 50 to 220 sheets of sandpaper, wrap a strip around a pencil and stroke off the rubber that is in the way. 50 grit will do most of the work in a few strokes and then 100, 180, and 220 grits will take you to the final smooth result. The fit should not be loose, just gently snug, like the original fit.<br />There you have it.<br />Your Arcitec will shave like a new RQ12**x and you have the reliability of the older, more stable, Li-Ion charging circuitry and all the convenience you have come to value in your Arcitec-x system.<br />If the battery should ever fail to hold or take a charge, you can replace it for $18 (ppd) via EBay. A screwdriver, small soldering iron, and a pair of scissors are all that's required.<br />When necessary, I will do that myself as well, and post the procedure.<br />Happy shaving.<br /><br />Update: It has been several weeks since I began using the RQ12 head on my Arcitec and I must say that I am even more favorably impressed that I was initially. For one thing, the battery in my Arcitec seems to last longer than it did with the old shaving head. Youcan attribute this to decreased friction in the newly designed RQ12 head, or decreased shaving time per session. Maybe both.<br /><br />Speaking of which, I believe I have discovered the reason Norelco asks it's new customers to go 21 days before making a decision about whether of not they like their new shaver. Although the stated reason is that one's beard needs to become accustomed to the new shaving pattern, my experience is that it takes a couple of weeks for the new cutting heads to \\"seat\\" properly, giving a better shearing action and therefore, a smoother, quicker shave.<br />Am I pleased? You bet I am!<br />I'll restate my original recommendation: If you have a working Arcitec, don't upgrade to a new 2012 RQ system. Instead, just buy a new RQ12 head for your already excellent Arcitec. The older battery/charging system is a apparently better than the finicky new system, and, powering the more efficient cutting RQ12 head, the battery will probably last as long as the driving motor.<br /><br />Cheaper, better, sounds like a win-win to me!
